<p><b>Linus Benedict Torvalds</b><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (born 28 December 1969) is a Finnish and American software engineer who is the creator and lead developer of the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a> since 1991. He also created the <a href="/wiki/Distributed_version_control" title="Distributed version control">distributed version control</a> system <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a>.
</p><p>Torvalds was one of the recipients of the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Technology_Prize" title="Millennium Technology Prize">Millennium Technology Prize</a> "in recognition of his creation of a new <a href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> for <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a> leading to the widely used Linux <a href="/wiki/Kernel_(operating_system)" title="Kernel (operating system)">kernel</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He is also the recipient of the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Computer_Pioneer_Award" title="Computer Pioneer Award">IEEE Computer Society Computer Pioneer Award</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the 2018 <a href="/wiki/IEEE_Masaru_Ibuka_Consumer_Electronics_Award" title="IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award">IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ibuka&#95;rl&#95;7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibuka_rl-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Life_and_career">Life and career</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_years">Early years</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Torvalds was born in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, on 28 December 1969, the son of journalists Anna and <a href="/wiki/Nils_Torvalds" title="Nils Torvalds">Nils Torvalds</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the grandson of statistician <a href="/wiki/Leo_T%C3%B6rnqvist" title="Leo Törnqvist">Leo Törnqvist</a> and of poet <a href="/wiki/Ole_Torvalds" title="Ole Torvalds">Ole Torvalds</a>, and the great-grandson of journalist and soldier <a href="/wiki/Toivo_Karanko" title="Toivo Karanko">Toivo Karanko</a>. His parents were campus radicals at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Helsinki" title="University of Helsinki">University of Helsinki</a> in the 1960s. His family belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Swedish-speaking_Finns" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish-speaking Finns">Swedish-speaking minority</a> in Finland. He was named after <a href="/wiki/Linus_Pauling" title="Linus Pauling">Linus Pauling</a>, the Nobel Prize-winning American chemist, although in the book <i><a href="/wiki/Rebel_Code" title="Rebel Code">Rebel Code: Linux and the Open Source Revolution</a></i>, he is quoted as saying, "I think I was named equally for <a href="/wiki/Linus_van_Pelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Linus van Pelt">Linus</a> the <i><a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a></i> cartoon character", noting that this made him "half Nobel Prize–winning chemist and half blanket-carrying cartoon character".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-moody&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moody-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>His interest in computers began with a <a href="/wiki/VIC-20" title="VIC-20">VIC-20</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> at the age of 11 in 1981. He started programming for it in <a href="/wiki/BASIC" title="BASIC">BASIC</a>, then later by directly accessing the <a href="/wiki/6502" class="mw-redirect" title="6502">6502</a> CPU directly in <a href="/wiki/Machine_code" title="Machine code">machine code</a> (rather than <a href="/wiki/Assembly_language" title="Assembly language">assembly language</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He then purchased a <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_QL" title="Sinclair QL">Sinclair QL</a>, which he modified extensively, especially its operating system. "Because it was so hard to get software for it in Finland", he wrote his own assembler and "(in addition to <a href="/wiki/Pac-Man" title="Pac-Man">Pac-Man</a> graphics libraries)"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for the QL, and a few games.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He wrote a <i><a href="/wiki/Pac-Man" title="Pac-Man">Pac-Man</a></i> clone, <i>Cool Man</i>.
</p><p>Torvalds attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Helsinki" title="University of Helsinki">University of Helsinki</a> from 1988 to 1996,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> graduating with a master's degree in <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> from the NODES research group.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His academic career was interrupted after his first year of study when he joined the <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Navy" title="Finnish Navy">Finnish Navy</a> <a href="/wiki/Nyland_Brigade" title="Nyland Brigade">Nyland Brigade</a> in the summer of 1989, selecting the 11-month officer training program to fulfill the <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Finland" title="Conscription in Finland">mandatory military service of Finland</a>. He gained the rank of <a href="/wiki/Second_lieutenant" title="Second lieutenant">second lieutenant</a>, with the role of an <a href="/wiki/Artillery_observer" title="Artillery observer">artillery observer</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1990, Torvalds resumed his university studies, and was exposed to Unix for the first time in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Digital_Equipment_Corporation" title="Digital Equipment Corporation">DEC</a> <a href="/wiki/MicroVAX" title="MicroVAX">MicroVAX</a> running <a href="/wiki/ULTRIX" class="mw-redirect" title="ULTRIX">ULTRIX</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later, he bought computer science professor <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Tanenbaum" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Tanenbaum">Andrew Tanenbaum</a>'s book <i><a href="/wiki/Operating_Systems:_Design_and_Implementation" title="Operating Systems: Design and Implementation">Operating Systems: Design and Implementation</a></i>, in which Tanenbaum describes <a href="/wiki/MINIX" class="mw-redirect" title="MINIX">MINIX</a>, an educational stripped-down version of <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 January 1991<sup id="cite&#95;ref-first&#95;interview&#95;20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-first_interview-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> he purchased an <a href="/wiki/Intel_80386" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel 80386">Intel 80386</a>-based <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC_clone" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM PC clone">IBM PC clone</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> before receiving a copy of <a href="/wiki/MINIX" class="mw-redirect" title="MINIX">MINIX</a>, which in turn enabled him to begin work on Linux.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Linux">Linux</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Linux"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Linux" title="History of Linux">History of Linux</a></div>
<p>The first Linux prototypes were publicly released on the Internet in late 1991 from an <a href="/wiki/FTP_server" title="FTP server">FTP server</a> at his university.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-moody&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moody-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Version 1.0 was released on 14 March 1994.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-kern1p0-release&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kern1p0-release-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Torvalds first encountered the <a href="/wiki/GNU_Project" title="GNU Project">GNU Project</a> in the autumn of 1991 when another Swedish-speaking computer science student, Lars Wirzenius, took him to the <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_University_of_Technology" title="Helsinki University of Technology">Helsinki University of Technology</a> to listen to free-software guru <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a>'s speech. Because of the talk and pressure from other contributors, Torvalds would ultimately switch his original license (which forbade commercial use) to Stallman's <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License_version_2" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU General Public License version 2">GNU General Public License version 2</a> (GPLv2) for his <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After a visit to <a href="/wiki/Transmeta" title="Transmeta">Transmeta</a> in late 1996,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-linuxonlinebio&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linuxonlinebio-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Torvalds accepted a position at the company in California, where he worked from February 1997 to June 2003. He then moved to the <a href="/wiki/Open_Source_Development_Labs" title="Open Source Development Labs">Open Source Development Labs</a>, which has since merged with the <a href="/wiki/Free_Standards_Group" title="Free Standards Group">Free Standards Group</a> to become the <a href="/wiki/Linux_Foundation" title="Linux Foundation">Linux Foundation</a>, under whose auspices he continues to work. In June 2004, Torvalds and his family moved to <a href="/wiki/Dunthorpe,_Oregon" title="Dunthorpe, Oregon">Dunthorpe, Oregon</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Rogoway&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogoway-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to be closer to the OSDL's headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Beaverton,_Oregon" title="Beaverton, Oregon">Beaverton</a>.
</p><p>From 1997 to 1999, he was involved in <a href="/wiki/86open" class="mw-redirect" title="86open">86open</a>, helping select the standard binary format for <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a>. In 1999, he was named by the <i><a href="/wiki/MIT_Technology_Review" title="MIT Technology Review">MIT Technology Review</a></i> <a href="/wiki/TR100" class="mw-redirect" title="TR100">TR100</a> as one of the world's top 100 innovators under age 35.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat" title="Red Hat">Red Hat</a> and <a href="/wiki/VA_Linux" class="mw-redirect" title="VA Linux">VA Linux</a>, both leading developers of Linux-based software, presented Torvalds with <a href="/wiki/Stock_option" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock option">stock options</a> in gratitude for his creation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-r1&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That year both companies <a href="/wiki/Went_public" class="mw-redirect" title="Went public">went public</a> and Torvalds's share value briefly shot up to about US$20&#160;million.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-unauthbio&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unauthbio-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>His personal mascot is a penguin nicknamed <a href="/wiki/Tux_(mascot)" title="Tux (mascot)">Tux</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which has been widely adopted by the Linux community as the Linux kernel's mascot.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although Torvalds believes "<a href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> is the only right way to do software", he also has said that he uses the "best tool for the job", even if that includes <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary software</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He was criticized for his use and alleged advocacy of the proprietary <a href="/wiki/BitKeeper" title="BitKeeper">BitKeeper</a> software for version control in the Linux kernel. He subsequently wrote a free-software replacement for it called <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a>.
</p><p>In 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> of <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a>, proposed to Linus to work on <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, requiring him to stop his work on the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a>. Linus refused, also arguing that the <a href="/wiki/Mach_(kernel)" title="Mach (kernel)">Mach</a> kernel was too different from <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>.
</p><p>In 2008, Torvalds stated that he used the <a href="/wiki/Fedora_Linux" title="Fedora Linux">Fedora Linux</a> distribution because it had fairly good support for the <a href="/wiki/PowerPC" title="PowerPC">PowerPC</a> processor architecture, which he favored at the time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LinusFedora&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LinusFedora-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He confirmed this in a 2012 interview.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Torvalds abandoned GNOME for a while after the release of <a href="/wiki/GNOME_3.0" class="mw-redirect" title="GNOME 3.0">GNOME 3.0</a>, saying, "The developers have apparently decided that it's 'too complicated' to actually do real work on your desktop, and have decided to make it really annoying to do". He then switched to <a href="/wiki/Xfce" title="Xfce">Xfce</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2013, Torvalds resumed using GNOME, noting that "they have extensions now that are still much too hard to find; but with extensions you can make your desktop look almost as good as it used to look two years ago".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Linux_Foundation" title="Linux Foundation">Linux Foundation</a> currently sponsors Torvalds so he can work full-time on improving Linux.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, while giving a talk at <a href="/wiki/Aalto_University" title="Aalto University">Aalto University</a>, Torvalds said "fuck you" and raised his middle finger after criticizing the company <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a>, which specializes in GPU technology. He said Nvidia was, at the time, the single worst company he has dealt with in the development of the kernel. In the talk, he also discussed other elements of computing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Torvalds is known for vocally disagreeing with other developers on the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel_mailing_list" title="Linux kernel mailing list">Linux kernel mailing list</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Calling himself a "really unpleasant person", he explained, "I'd like to be a nice person and curse less and encourage people to grow rather than telling them they are idiots. I'm sorry—I tried, it's just not in me."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His attitude, which he considers necessary for making his points clear, has drawn criticism from <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> programmer <a href="/wiki/Sage_Sharp" title="Sage Sharp">Sage Sharp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Systemd" title="Systemd">systemd</a> developer <a href="/wiki/Lennart_Poettering" title="Lennart Poettering">Lennart Poettering</a>, among others.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2022)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On Sunday, 16 September 2018, the Linux kernel <i>Code of Conflict</i> was suddenly replaced by a new <i>Code of Conduct</i> based on the <a href="/wiki/Contributor_Covenant" title="Contributor Covenant">Contributor Covenant</a>. Shortly thereafter, in the release notes for Linux 4.19-rc4, Torvalds apologized for his behavior, calling his personal attacks of the past "unprofessional and uncalled for" and announced a period of "time off" to "get some assistance on how to understand people's emotions and respond appropriately". It soon transpired that these events followed <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> approaching Torvalds with a series of questions critical of his conduct.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Following the release of Linux 4.19 on 22 October 2018, Torvalds returned to maintaining the kernel.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2024, amidst the <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>, some developers were excluded from the list of Linux kernel maintainers, seemingly over being Russian or using Russian email addresses. Torvalds commented: "I'm Finnish. Did you think I'd be supporting Russian aggression?". Some developers, along with a part of Linux users, noted the lack of public clarity about that move. Later Torvalds claimed that he acted according to government compliance requirements and due to legal issues around Russia.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="The_Linus/Linux_connection"><span id="The_Linus.2FLinux_connection"></span>The Linus/Linux connection</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Linus/Linux connection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Linux#Naming" title="History of Linux">History of Linux §&#160;Naming</a></div>
<p>Initially, Torvalds wanted to call the kernel he developed <i>Freax</i> (a combination of "free", "freak", and the letter X to indicate that it was a Unix-like system), but his friend <a href="/wiki/Ari_Lemmke" class="mw-redirect" title="Ari Lemmke">Ari Lemmke</a>, who administered the <a href="/wiki/FTP_server" title="FTP server">FTP server</a> where the kernel was first hosted, named Torvalds' directory <i>linux</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Authority_and_trademark">Authority and trademark</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Authority and trademark"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>As of 2006, approximately 2% of the Linux kernel was written by Torvalds.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-unauthbio&#95;30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unauthbio-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite the thousands who have contributed to it, his percentage is still one of the largest. However, he said in 2012 that his own personal contribution is now mostly merging code written by others, with little programming.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He retains the highest authority to decide which new code is incorporated into the standard Linux kernel.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Torvalds holds the <i>Linux</i> trademark<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and monitors its use,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> chiefly through the <a href="/wiki/Linux_Mark_Institute" title="Linux Mark Institute">Linux Mark Institute</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Other_software">Other software</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other software"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Other&#95;apps"></span>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Git">Git</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Git"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Git#History" title="Git">Git §&#160;History</a></div>
<p>On 3 April 2005, Torvalds began development on <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a>, <a href="/wiki/Version_control_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Version control software">version control software</a> that later became widely used. 
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Subsurface&#95;(software)"></span>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Subsurface">Subsurface</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Subsurface"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Subsurface is software for logging and planning <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba dives</a>, which Torvalds began developing in late 2011. It is <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open_source_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Free and open source software">free and open source software</a> distributed under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License_version_2" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU General Public License version 2">GNU General Public License version 2</a>. Dirk Hohndel became its head maintainer in late 2012.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sparse">Sparse</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sparse"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Sparse"></span>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sparse" title="Sparse">Sparse</a></div>
<p>Sparse is a <a href="/wiki/Static_code_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Static code analysis">static analysis</a> tool that flags constructs that are likely to be of interest to <a href="/wiki/Kernel_(operating_system)" title="Kernel (operating system)">kernel</a> developers, such as the mixing of pointers to user and kernel <a href="/wiki/Address_space" title="Address space">address spaces</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Personal_life">Personal life</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal life"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Linus_Torvalds.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Linus_Torvalds.jpeg/250px-Linus_Torvalds.jpeg" decoding="async" width="175" height="239" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Linus_Torvalds.jpeg/500px-Linus_Torvalds.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="819" /></a><figcaption>Torvalds in 2002</figcaption></figure>
<p>Linus Torvalds is married to Tove Torvalds (<span title="Name at birth"><a href="/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names" title="Birth name">née</a>&#160;Monni</span>), a six-time Finnish national <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a> champion, whom he met in late 1993. He was running introductory computer laboratory exercises for students and instructed the course attendees to send him an e-mail as a test, to which Tove responded with an e-mail asking for a date.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-moody&#95;9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moody-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They were later married and have three daughters, two of whom were born in the United States.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-oreg100914&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oreg100914-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Linux kernel's <i>reboot</i> system call accepts their dates of birth (written in hexadecimal) as <a href="/wiki/Magic_number_(programming)" title="Magic number (programming)">magic values</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-reboot2&#95;63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reboot2-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Torvalds has described himself as "completely <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">a-religious</a>—<a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a>", adding, "I find that people seem to think religion brings morals and appreciation of nature. I actually think it detracts from both. It gives people the excuse to say, 'Oh, nature was just created,' and so the act of creation is seen to be something miraculous. I appreciate the fact that, 'Wow, it's incredible that something like this could have happened in the first place.<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>" He later added that while in Europe religion is mostly a personal issue, in the United States it has become very politicized. When discussing the issue of <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">church and state separation</a>, he said, "Yeah, it's kind of ironic that in many European countries, there is actually a kind of legal binding between the state and the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In "Linus the Liberator", a story about the March <a href="/wiki/LinuxWorld_Conference_and_Expo" title="LinuxWorld Conference and Expo">LinuxWorld Conference</a>, Torvalds says: "There are like two golden rules in life. One is 'Do unto others as you would want them to do unto you.' For some reason, people associate this with Christianity. I'm not a Christian. I'm agnostic. The other rule is 'Be proud of what you do.<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, Torvalds moved with his family from <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> to <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, Torvalds became a United States citizen and <a href="/wiki/Voter_registration_in_the_United_States" title="Voter registration in the United States">registered to vote in the United States</a>. As of that year, he was unaffiliated with any U.S. political party, saying, "I have way too much personal pride to want to be associated with any of them, quite frankly."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-oreg100914&#95;61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oreg100914-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Linus developed an interest in <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> in the early 2000s and has achieved numerous certifications, leading him to create the Subsurface project.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Awards_and_achievements">Awards and achievements</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Awards and achievements"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Linus-Torvalds_IEEE_Ibuka_Award_2018.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Linus-Torvalds_IEEE_Ibuka_Award_2018.jpg/250px-Linus-Torvalds_IEEE_Ibuka_Award_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Linus-Torvalds_IEEE_Ibuka_Award_2018.jpg/500px-Linus-Torvalds_IEEE_Ibuka_Award_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5272" data-file-height="3304" /></a><figcaption>Linus Torvalds (centre) receiving the 2018 <a href="/wiki/IEEE_Masaru_Ibuka_Consumer_Electronics_Award" title="IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award">IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award</a> from ICCE 2018 Conference Chair <a href="/wiki/Saraju_Mohanty" title="Saraju Mohanty">Saraju Mohanty</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/IEEE" class="mw-redirect" title="IEEE">IEEE</a> President James A. Jefferies (right) at ICCE 2018 on 12 January 2018 in Las Vegas</figcaption></figure>

<td>IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/IEEE_Masaru_Ibuka_Consumer_Electronics_Award" title="IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award">IEEE Masaru Ibuka Consumer Electronics Award</a> is conferred by the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers" title="Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers">Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers</a> for outstanding contributions to consumer electronics technology has been named in honor of the co-founder and honorary chairman of Sony Corporation, Masaru Ibuka. 2018 Ibuka award was conferred to Linus Torvalds "For his leadership of the development and proliferation of Linux."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ibuka&#95;rl&#95;7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibuka_rl-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

<td>2014
</td>
<td>IEEE Computer Pioneer Award
</td>
<td>On 23 April 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers" title="Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers">Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers</a> named Torvalds as the 2014 recipient of the IEEE Computer Society's <a href="/wiki/Computer_Pioneer_Award" title="Computer Pioneer Award">Computer Pioneer Award</a>. The Computer Pioneer Award was established in 1981 by the IEEE Computer Society Board of Governors to recognize and honor the vision of those whose efforts resulted in the creation and continued vitality of the computer industry. The award is presented to outstanding individuals whose main contribution to the concepts and development of the computer field was made at least 15 years earlier.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>

<td>2012
</td>
<td>Internet Hall of Fame
</td>
<td>On 23 April 2012, at <a href="/wiki/Internet_Society" title="Internet Society">Internet Society</a>'s Global INET conference in Geneva, Switzerland, Torvalds was one of the inaugural inductees into the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Hall_of_Fame" title="Internet Hall of Fame">Internet Hall of Fame</a>, one of ten in the Innovators category and thirty-three overall inductees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>2012
</td>
<td>Millennium Technology Prize
</td>
<td>On 20 April 2012, Torvalds was declared one of two winners of that year's <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Technology_Prize" title="Millennium Technology Prize">Millennium Technology Prize</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Shinya_Yamanaka" title="Shinya Yamanaka">Shinya Yamanaka</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The honor is widely described as technology's equivalent of the Nobel Prize.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>2010
</td>
<td>C&amp;C Prize
</td>
<td>He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/C%26C_Prize" title="C&amp;C Prize">C&amp;C Prize</a> by the <a href="/wiki/NEC_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="NEC Corporation">NEC Corporation</a> in 2010 for "contributions to the advancement of the information technology industry, education, research, and the improvement of our lives".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>2008
</td>
<td>Hall of Fellows
</td>

</td></tr>

</td>
<td>Vollum Award
</td>
<td>In August 2005, Torvalds received the <a href="/wiki/Howard_Vollum" title="Howard Vollum">Vollum Award</a> from <a href="/wiki/Reed_College" title="Reed College">Reed College</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>2003
</td>
<td>Linus (Moon)
</td>
<td>In 2003, the naming of the asteroid moon <a href="/wiki/Linus_(moon)" title="Linus (moon)">Linus</a> was motivated in part by the fact that the discoverer was an enthusiastic Linux user. Although the naming proposal referred to the mythological <a href="/wiki/Linus_(mythology)" title="Linus (mythology)">Linus</a>, son of the muse <a href="/wiki/Calliope" title="Calliope">Calliope</a> and the inventor of melody and rhythm, the name was also meant to honor Linus Torvalds, and <a href="/wiki/Linus_van_Pelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Linus van Pelt">Linus van Pelt</a>, a character in the <i><a href="/wiki/Peanuts" title="Peanuts">Peanuts</a></i> comic strip.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</td></tr>

</td>

</td>

</td></tr>

</td></tr>

</td>

</td>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>1997
</td>
<td>Academic Honors
</td>
<td>In 1997, Torvalds received his master's degree (Laudatur Grade) from the Department of Computer Science at the University of Helsinki. Two years later he received honorary doctor status at <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_University" title="Stockholm University">Stockholm University</a>, and in 2000, he received the same honor from his <i>alma mater</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<p>University of Helsinki has named an auditorium after Torvalds and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cs.helsinki.fi/u/kutvonen/index_files/humalluoto.html">his computer</a> is on display at the Department of Computer Science.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Media_recognition">Media recognition</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Linus_Torvalds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Media recognition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i> magazine</a> has recognized Torvalds multiple times:
</p>
<ul><li>In 2000, he was 17th in their <a href="/wiki/Time_100:_The_Most_Important_People_of_the_Century" title="Time 100: The Most Important People of the Century">Time 100: The Most Important People of the Century</a> poll.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, he was named one of the most influential people in the world by <i>Time</i> magazine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2006, the magazine's Europe edition named him one of the revolutionary heroes of the past 60 years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-r1&#95;28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/InfoWorld" title="InfoWorld">InfoWorld</a></i> presented him with the 2000 Award for Industry Achievement.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2005, Torvalds appeared as one of "the best managers" in a survey by <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect" title="BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Business_2.0" title="Business 2.0">Business 2.0</a></i> magazine named him one of "10 people who don't matter" because the growth of Linux has shrunk Torvalds's individual impact.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In summer 2004, viewers of <a href="/wiki/YLE" class="mw-redirect" title="YLE">YLE</a> (the Finnish Broadcasting Company) placed Torvalds 16th in the network's <a href="/wiki/Suuret_Suomalaiset" class="mw-redirect" title="Suuret Suomalaiset">100 Greatest Finns</a>. In 2010, as part of a series called <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica,_Inc." title="Encyclopædia Britannica, Inc.">The Britannica Guide</a> to the World's Most Influential People</i>, Torvalds was listed among <i>The 100 Most Influential Inventors of All Time</i> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1333433106">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit;word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}.mw-parser-output a,.mw-parser-output .id-lock-registration.id-lock-registration a{background:url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output
